< review>
We had so much fun this morning with our two dogs. There's a short 1/3 mile path around the dog plus a kid playground and benches. Then there's the dog park towards the front of the park. There's two areas--the small dog area is all grass and has a small pool, and the all dog area is half grass and half dirt with another small pool. There's a few trees for shade too. There's a drinking station and poop bags and cans. We went early on Sunday and there were dozens of dogs and humans there but it didn't feel crowded at all. It was the first time I took my puppy to a dog park and it was a good experience for her because all the owners were responsible and attentive. We'll definitely be back again!< /review>

< review>
The park is good sized. There are 2 fenced off, off leash dog parks, one for bigger dogs that has a couple of benches. Its 3/4ths dirt and the rest is grass. Than there is a smaller fenced off grassy area for smaller dogs. The rest of the park is good sized, huge grassy area with trees for shade with benches and one or two charcoal bbqs. There's also a cement path that circles around the whole park. The kids playground is pretty nice as well in a sand pit area. There are men and women bathrooms which are usually pretty clean. The parking lot is pretty well lit as well.</review>

< review>
This park is nice for the kids and dogs for a short period. 1 playground, a few grills, a few benches, many small immature tree's, 2 dog parks with water spouts for dog drinking, and public bathrooms with 2 drinking fountains and a concrete track for walking (.5 mile maybe). The playground has baby and kids swings (4 altogether) and 4 climbing jungle gym thingamagigs (these are fun for the kids). I frequent as I live in Palmdale and own a dog. Close, convenient and clean. Always manicured and dog owners tend to pickup after their dogs waste.</review>

<review>Great place for both pet lovers and family. Two separate dog areas; larger area for larger dogs and the non-shy smaller ones, and a smaller area for the small dogs and the shy larger ones. Everyone is quite friendly in both areas, as long as you mind your pet and your kids. Some owners do not appreciate when others do not mind their pets, and their pets become overly playful; some dogs do not do well with that type of play, and those with very playful pups should be respectful of that.

Play area for the kids is great; newer equipment that keeps the kids moving and interested for a good amount of time.

The rest of the park is a large grassy area that has a walking/jogging path around it for those who want to walk their dogs or get in some exercise. It also has a couple areas for bbq'ing and the grass areas allow for soccer games, football games, etc.

The only downside that I can find at the park is that some parents opt to ignore the no skateboard/rollerblades/bike riding policy within the park, and allow their kids to do these activities. Which, unfortunately, is very bothersome to the people who are jogging, walking their dogs (which become very scared or irritated), and following the rules.<//review><Name>Kimberlee Redding< /Name>< resp>
None< /resp>

< review>
Professional, quick and effective (Eastbay)

I had a 200,000 gallon water leak that resulted in an extremely high water bill.  Though I am extremely familiar with my irrigation system and visually checked my property, I could not see any evidence of a huge leak.
When they arrived on site, they did double check that the leak was in the irrigation line and not the line to the house and even checked each valve to make sure there was no stuck valve or problem in the irrigation boxes.  Within the hour they were able of mark the site of the leak using pressurized gas and water combination and marked the location for me. Scott and XXX were very polite and did not mind me asking many questions and following them around.

The report was sent the next day with photos and showing where they located the leak.  I had the spot dig up just this weekend.  Though the leak was visibly undetectable, it is located under driveway pavers approximately 2 feet deep.  The spot they marked was within 4 foot square of the mark. As we dug to 1.5 feet deep turning on the irrigation main allowed the water to spray out and find the leak which was a huge help on an over Â½ acre property.

< Review>
Back in February, I was looking in particular for a Dodge Ram 2500 regular cab with the 5.9 L diesel.  The regular cab is hard to find for the most part.  I am in CA, 20 minutes from the Oregon border, so the choices were limited.  I found the exact model (with a camper shell as a bonus) at Elite Motors while searching the Internet.  Called and talked to Matt and he said he would keep it on hold for me while I drove down the next day.

The Elite Motors dealership is very clean and both Matt and Tom were excellent people to work with.  I have a close friend in the car business, so I am familiar with how things work when buying a used car.  I could see a number of quality vehicles on the lot and just wish that the dealership was  not so far away when I go to look for a car for my daughter.

Finally, it has been almost 3 months and 3,000 miles later (one really long trip in the mix) and the truck is just wonderful.  My thanks to Elite Motors for having it on the lot when I really needed to replace my aging work truck.  Thanks again, Matt!< /Review>

Cal., and, myself, hunted ground squirrels and whatever other target crossed my path, considered myself informed of the current rules and regulations. Of course that was 60+ years ago! <username>James Whitehouse<//username>< Text>
The class was good, but there were too many people, the room and range were too warm, and the walls of the classroom are too thin.  It made it difficult to hear Mike and Glen give instruction.  Overall, the instruction and qualification is what I expected.  However, I disagreed with parts regarding what to tell law enforcement in the event of an incident, as well as what force is needed to "stop the threat" for a CCW holding member of the public (MOP).  I doubt anyone in the class besides the instructor Glen had done a felony car stop and engaged someone with a firearm.  A MOP is likely to unload on someone and it is not because they want to "get their gun off," it is because of adrenaline.  I also think it would have been good to advise students to carry a tactical flashlight, an extra magazine, a knife, and a less than lethal alternative.  From a practical and legal standpoint, carrying these things opens up defensive arguments for MOPS involved in the use of lethal/ "enough to stop the threat" force.< /Text>

< Review>
For this past Mother's Day my husband bought me a gun, we both thought it would be a good idea to do a CCW class. A few days later one of our friends mentioned he was setting up a group who also wanted to either get their initial CCW or get a refresher course.
We were both super excited, however I was a little nervous. I had been to an indoor range a number of times but have never actually loaded my own gun; I had always gone with friends who would do that and hand it over for me to try to shoot the target.
After the first 2 nights of class I felt so much better about handling, transporting, and maintaining my gun and I hadn't even shot it yet! Ted and Mike did such a wonderful job at keeping the class entertaining and explaining things so that everyone could understand; whether you were a beginner like myself or an advanced shooter.
When we got to the range I was so nervous. I was going to shoot my gun. I was so impressed by how Ted and Mike seemed to make that all go away. They did such a fantastic job at giving each and every individual the help they needed. I have a "harder" time taking direction however I never once felt like either Ted or Mike were annoyed by consistently helping or answering any questions I had. Throughout our time at the range I felt my confidence in my ability to handle my gun grow. It is such a cool feeling.
I plan to continue practicing shooting and the maneuvers we were taught by NFI; maybe one day it will save my life.< /Review>

< text>
I was a student in the Hunters' Safety Course hosted by Ted Lidie at Sportsmans' Warehouse in Redding. To start out with in the class Ted asked us all of our names and memorized them. He continued to call each of us by name throughout the duration of the class. I thought this was a great personal touch that made everyone more comfortable in the classroom.  Ted was great at helping out the younger kids without giving away free answers to them. He answered all the questions they had and never once belittled or talked down to them unlike other firearms instrcutors I have had in the past. I sure hope that he is still teaching when my kids are ready to start hunting. As for the course material, I learned a ton and built a solid foundation to pass the test. I passed with a 97%.  I feel that Ted is the perfect person to introduce someone into hunting simply because he is so passionate about it and wants everyone to have a good, safe time. Thank you for your service Ted and God Bless!< /text>

<text>So, I hate writing reviews, because honestly, i feel it as the same at voting my 1 review does not make a difference. but as for Ted, I want to write a review!

I am not surprised he has 5 stars he is awesome. On wednesday I received my ccw request for a class. I liked guns fishing and other stuff so decided to give Ted a call, off the bat he gave me the info i needed. cool I will go there.

I went there yesterday in the class, and honestly i was kind of nervous, wondering what is this class going to entail? i wasn't good at school will i learn much? what if i fail? what if today i cant shoot? Ted came in the class and he came up and started talking.

Amazingly, how he explained everything I understood everything I needed to and more. such as, if what positions would it be acceptable to use a firearm. either way to get to the point his references did not make it feel like a class, it felt as if you were learning from a professional friend. We all have that friend that tells us laws and then you find out they were wrong.... This wasn't the case, Ted knows his stuff.

I went to the range the day before shooting straight, last couple weeks before shooting straight, no problems. I have no idea why but yesterday I could not shoot for the life of me... don't know why, but Ted didnt yell, he didnt even look at me like "geeze this guy sucks" he told me what I was doing and told me to keep trying.

Eventually i got back in my groove, didnt shoot as good as i normally, but better than i started. The whole time he made me feel comfortable. Whether i shot good or bad i felt good.

This is probably the longest review I ever wrote, but point being Ted is awesome. I hope other people get to experience what I did yesterday. I cant say how other instructors are, but I know I probably wont, because I will probably look for any more classes Ted has in the area if I take another class of anything. I plan on purchasing a smaller barrel gun and look forward to seeing Ted to take another class.

Hope this helped at least 1 person.

-Andrew Kim<//text><pics>None<//pics><resp>None< /resp><gmapID>0x54d2ecba3e3e183f:0x9c02f88e5c3f72df< /gmapID></record>
